<a id='comment:1'></a>
In Debian we already have giac 1.6.0-7 and one doctest either times out or segfaults. If it does not time out it looks as below. With the giac 1.5.0-87 Debian package the test works fine.

```
sage -t --long --random-seed=0 sage/src/sage/rings/polynomial/multi_polynomial_ideal.py
**********************************************************************
File "sage/src/sage/rings/polynomial/multi_polynomial_ideal.py", line 2101, in sage.rings.polynomial.multi_polynomial_ideal.?.elimination_ideal
Failed example:
    I.elimination_ideal([t, s], algorithm="giac") == J
Exception raised:
    Traceback (most recent call last):

<a id='comment:9'></a>
Build fails on macOS with

```
[giac-1.6.0.17p0] /bin/bash: hevea: command not found
```
Hoping that upstream can improve the autoconf tests a bit by the time that we are ready to do the giac 1.6 upgrade in the Sage 9.3 cycle.

We also have a number of patches in `build/pkgs/giac/patches` that can hopefully be upstreamed...

<a id='comment:11'></a>
I have a failure when I ran the testsuite on Gentoo

```
======================================
   giac 1.6.0: check/test-suite.log
======================================

# TOTAL: 30
# PASS:  29
# SKIP:  0
# XFAIL: 0
# FAIL:  1
# XPASS: 0
# ERROR: 0

.. contents:: :depth: 2

FAIL: chk_fhan11
================

// Using locale /usr/share/locale/
// C
// /usr/share/locale/
// giac

archive/issue_comments_489770.json:
```json
{
    "body": "<a id='comment:27'></a>\nWe are now at giac-1.6.0.41 and in keeping with upstream's habit, this has big changes that should be a major release.\n* it ships and uses micropython - 1.6.0.37 from a few days earlier has the source too.\n* in this release, xcas bits are built with micropython and it seems impossible to build giac without enabling gui and using fltk. Whether or not you enabled `gui`, bits of xcas are built and the build will fails without fltk being properly detected at configuration time.\n\nEffectively `--disable-gui` is not an option in this release. \n\n1.6.0.37 could still build with `--disable-gui` but I had one test failure in `chk_xavier` which does now pass in 1.6.0.41.",
    "created_at": "2020-12-15T22:46:18Z",
    "issue": "https://github.com/sagemath/sage/issues/30537",
    "type": "issue_comment",
    "url": "https://github.com/sagemath/sage/issues/30537#issuecomment-489770",
    "user": "https://github.com/kiwifb"
}
```

<a id='comment:27'></a>
We are now at giac-1.6.0.41 and in keeping with upstream's habit, this has big changes that should be a major release.
* it ships and uses micropython - 1.6.0.37 from a few days earlier has the source too.
* in this release, xcas bits are built with micropython and it seems impossible to build giac without enabling gui and using fltk. Whether or not you enabled `gui`, bits of xcas are built and the build will fails without fltk being properly detected at configuration time.

Effectively `--disable-gui` is not an option in this release. 

1.6.0.37 could still build with `--disable-gui` but I had one test failure in `chk_xavier` which does now pass in 1.6.0.41.



---

archive/issue_comments_489775.json:
```json
{
    "body": "<a id='comment:32'></a>\nMicroPython is not used at all for giac. Giac is used inside the builtin Micropython modules provided by this Giac distribution. This gives the same implementation of MicroPython across several ports targetted for educationnal use, with compatibility:\\\\\n1/ Xcas, \\\\\n2/ Xcas for Firefox [https://www-fourier.univ-grenoble-alpes.fr/~parisse/xcasen.html](https://www-fourier.univ-grenoble-alpes.fr/~parisse/xcasen.html) (with Python enabled [https://www-fourier.univ-grenoble-alpes.fr/~parisse/xcasen.html#python=4](https://www-fourier.univ-grenoble-alpes.fr/~parisse/xcasen.html#python=4))\\\\\n3/ tableaunoirxcas a blackboard for online teaching where you can insert Xcas, MicroPython or Javascript magnets\n[https://www-fourier.univ-grenoble-alpes.fr/~parisse/tableaunoirxcas/index.html](https://www-fourier.univ-grenoble-alpes.fr/~parisse/tableaunoirxcas/index.html)\nexample [https://www-fourier.univ-grenoble-alpes.fr/~parisse/tableaunoirxcas/#mat309/myblackboard.tableaunoir](https://www-fourier.univ-grenoble-alpes.fr/~parisse/tableaunoirxcas/#mat309/myblackboard.tableaunoir)\\\\\n4/ KhiCAS for the Numworks N0110, TI Nspire CX and CX II calculators.\\\\\nCPython can not be used on calculators because of the low ressources available (256K of RAM on the Numworks).",

<a id='comment:32'></a>
MicroPython is not used at all for giac. Giac is used inside the builtin Micropython modules provided by this Giac distribution. This gives the same implementation of MicroPython across several ports targetted for educationnal use, with compatibility:\\
1/ Xcas, \\
2/ Xcas for Firefox [https://www-fourier.univ-grenoble-alpes.fr/~parisse/xcasen.html](https://www-fourier.univ-grenoble-alpes.fr/~parisse/xcasen.html) (with Python enabled [https://www-fourier.univ-grenoble-alpes.fr/~parisse/xcasen.html#python=4](https://www-fourier.univ-grenoble-alpes.fr/~parisse/xcasen.html#python=4))\\
3/ tableaunoirxcas a blackboard for online teaching where you can insert Xcas, MicroPython or Javascript magnets
[https://www-fourier.univ-grenoble-alpes.fr/~parisse/tableaunoirxcas/index.html](https://www-fourier.univ-grenoble-alpes.fr/~parisse/tableaunoirxcas/index.html)
example [https://www-fourier.univ-grenoble-alpes.fr/~parisse/tableaunoirxcas/#mat309/myblackboard.tableaunoir](https://www-fourier.univ-grenoble-alpes.fr/~parisse/tableaunoirxcas/#mat309/myblackboard.tableaunoir)\\
4/ KhiCAS for the Numworks N0110, TI Nspire CX and CX II calculators.\\
CPython can not be used on calculators because of the low ressources available (256K of RAM on the Numworks).

Replying to [mkoeppe](#comment%3A36):
> on macOS:
> 
> ```
> [giac-1.6.0.47p0] gcc  -fPIC -DMICROPY_LIB -I. -I.. -I../py -Ibuild -Wall  -ansi -std=gnu99 -DFFCONF_H=\"lib/oofatfs/ffconf.h\" -g   -c -MD -o build/py/asmx86.o ../py/asmx86.c
> [giac-1.6.0.47p0] ../py/compile.c:1127:27: error: implicitly declaring library function 'alloca' with type 'void *(unsigned long)' [-Werror,-Wimplicit-function-declaration]
> [giac-1.6.0.47p0]             char *q_ptr = mp_local_alloc(len);
> [giac-1.6.0.47p0]                           ^
> [giac-1.6.0.47p0] ../py/pystack.h:78:33: note: expanded from macro 'mp_local_alloc'
> [giac-1.6.0.47p0] #define mp_local_alloc(n_bytes) alloca(n_bytes)
> [giac-1.6.0.47p0]                                 ^
> [giac-1.6.0.47p0] ../py/compile.c:1127:27: note: include the header <stdlib.h> or explicitly provide a declaration for 'alloca'
> [giac-1.6.0.47p0] ../py/pystack.h:78:33: note: expanded from macro 'mp_local_alloc'
> [giac-1.6.0.47p0] #define mp_local_alloc(n_bytes) alloca(n_bytes)

2/ pari: what should I add in configure.ac?
3/ gbasis/eliminate: maybe, you can modify your test and add gbasis as additional argument to your command. By default, eliminate does not compute a gbasis if there is only 1 variable to eliminate, resultant is more efficient.

<a id='comment:65'></a>
But I don't know how to adapt this inside my configure.ac. Current code slice is

```
CONFIG_PARI="yes"
AC_ARG_ENABLE([pari],
	[AS_HELP_STRING([--enable-pari], [Use PARI [[default=yes]]])],
	[ if test "$enableval" = "no"; then CONFIG_PARI="no"; fi], [])
  
if test "$CONFIG_PARI" = "yes"; then
	AC_CHECK_HEADERS(pari/pari.h, [], [CONFIG_PARI="no"])
fi
if test "$CONFIG_PARI" = "yes"; then
	save_LIBS="$LIBS"
	AC_CHECK_LIB(pari, main, [], [CONFIG_PARI="no"])
	LIBS="$save_LIBS"
  fi
PARI_LIBS=""
if test "$CONFIG_PARI" = "yes"; then
	PARI_LIBS="-lpari"
fi
AC_SUBST(PARI_LIBS)
AC_SUBST(CONFIG_PARI)
AM_CONDITIONAL(CONFIG_PARI, [test "$CONFIG_PARI" = "yes"])

```

<a id='comment:67'></a>
Replying to [parisse](#comment%3A65):
> But I don't know how to adapt this inside my configure.ac. Current code slice is
> 
> ```
> CONFIG_PARI="yes"
> AC_ARG_ENABLE([pari],
> 	[AS_HELP_STRING([--enable-pari], [Use PARI [[default=yes]]])],
> 	[ if test "$enableval" = "no"; then CONFIG_PARI="no"; fi], [])
>   
> if test "$CONFIG_PARI" = "yes"; then
> 	AC_CHECK_HEADERS(pari/pari.h, [], [CONFIG_PARI="no"])
> fi
> if test "$CONFIG_PARI" = "yes"; then
> 	save_LIBS="$LIBS"
> 	AC_CHECK_LIB(pari, main, [], [CONFIG_PARI="no"])
> 	LIBS="$save_LIBS"
>   fi
> ```


Add the following here:

```
+ if test "$CONFIG_PARI" = "yes"; then
+                     AC_MSG_CHECKING([whether PARI is configured with pthreads])
+                     AC_RUN_IFELSE([AC_LANG_PROGRAM([
+                         [#include <pari/pari.h>
+                          #include <string.h>]],
+                        [[return strcmp(PARI_MT_ENGINE, "pthread") != 0]])],
+                       [AC_MSG_RESULT([yes. Good])],
+                       [AC_MSG_RESULT([no. Not good])
+                        CONFIG_PARI="no"])
+ fi
```

> ```
> PARI_LIBS=""
> if test "$CONFIG_PARI" = "yes"; then
> 	PARI_LIBS="-lpari"
> fi
> AC_SUBST(PARI_LIBS)
> AC_SUBST(CONFIG_PARI)
> AM_CONDITIONAL(CONFIG_PARI, [test "$CONFIG_PARI" = "yes"])
> 
> ```

archive/issue_comments_489851.json:
```json
{
    "body": "<a id='comment:94'></a>\nOK, so the last bit of difference seems to be that internal representation in giac has changed. Looking at the larger context of the doctest\n\n```\n    def eval(self, code, strip=True, **kwds):\n        r\"\"\"\n        Send the code x to the Giac interpreter.\n        Remark: To enable multi-lines codes in the notebook magic mode: ``%giac``,\n        the ``\\n`` are removed before sending the code to giac.\n        INPUT:\n        - code -- str\n        - strip -- Default is True and removes ``\\n``\n        EXAMPLES::\n            sage: giac.eval(\"2+2;\\n3\")\n            '4,3'\n            sage: giac.eval(\"2+2;\\n3\",False)\n            '4\\n3'\n            sage: s='g(x):={\\nx+1;\\nx+2;\\n}'\n            sage: giac(s)\n            (x)->[x+1,x+2]\n            sage: giac.g(5)\n            7\n        \"\"\"\n        #we remove \\n to enable multiline code in the notebook magic mode %giac\n```\nThe line `giac(s)` doesn't really show anything that interesting and could be either removed or marked random.",

    "user": "https://github.com/kiwifb"
}
```

<a id='comment:94'></a>
OK, so the last bit of difference seems to be that internal representation in giac has changed. Looking at the larger context of the doctest

```
    def eval(self, code, strip=True, **kwds):
        r"""
        Send the code x to the Giac interpreter.
        Remark: To enable multi-lines codes in the notebook magic mode: ``%giac``,
        the ``\n`` are removed before sending the code to giac.
        INPUT:
        - code -- str
        - strip -- Default is True and removes ``\n``
        EXAMPLES::
            sage: giac.eval("2+2;\n3")
            '4,3'
            sage: giac.eval("2+2;\n3",False)
            '4\n3'
            sage: s='g(x):={\nx+1;\nx+2;\n}'
            sage: giac(s)
            (x)->[x+1,x+2]
            sage: giac.g(5)
            7
        """
        #we remove \n to enable multiline code in the notebook magic mode %giac
```
The line `giac(s)` doesn't really show anything that interesting and could be either removed or marked random.



---

<a id='comment:4'></a>
I'd have to double check that. Some (mathematical) tests return different results depending on whether you build the GUI (linked to fltk) or not. The results distributed with giac are done with GUI. I officially gave up on patching for tests without GUI in sage-on-gentoo for giac-1.6.0-x, because it would have been a massive patch. Very much like what would be needed given your results above. I just cannot ascertain that it was `chk_fhan9` on top of my head.
